<div id="review_1877172141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1877172141" />
    <a title="Michael Britt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51188905-michael-britt"><img alt="Michael Britt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513347398p2/51188905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1877172141?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Britt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Britt" href="/user/show/51188905-michael-britt">Michael Britt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/30508032-the-bonehunters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51188905-michael-britt?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1877172141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4477343865335508758">I'm not really sure how much I can say without spoiling the book, so this will probably be a short review. We'll see. <br/><br/>I stated this all throughout my updates, but this is by far the best book in the series, so far. Up til this point, Memories of Ice was the only time that we've had more than a few characters come back. So it was awesome to see such a huge cast of characters that we're so familiar with make a comeback. For one, it helped the story be less confusing. Although, after Memories of Ic</span>
  <span id="freeText4477343865335508758" style="display:none">I'm not really sure how much I can say without spoiling the book, so this will probably be a short review. We'll see. <br /><br />I stated this all throughout my updates, but this is by far the best book in the series, so far. Up til this point, Memories of Ice was the only time that we've had more than a few characters come back. So it was awesome to see such a huge cast of characters that we're so familiar with make a comeback. For one, it helped the story be less confusing. Although, after Memories of Ice, it really hasn't been all that hard to follow along.<br /><br />Erikson's writing in this book is just above and beyond. The pacing and character development were superb. It never once felt like the story got stagnant. This installment and Memories of Ice were honestly the only 2 that I never got bored during. That's not a jab at Erikson: with characters that are as grey as these, you almost need a lot of internal dialogue to help you understand why they do what they do. But that can get boring, sometimes. So, I came to grips with that fact a long time ago. It was awesome to get a book where you never felt that boredom. There is still quite a bit of inner dialogue, but it felt different this time. Maybe due to where they were at in the story? No idea. I will say that I'm ecstatic to get to our battle royale between 3 certain warriors. That's all I can really say without spoiler tags. <br /><br />The characters in this book were what helped make this book as great as it was. We were also introduced to a few smaller characters. Grub and Chaur becoming some of my favorite of the minor cast. We also get some great insight into T'Amber, and she might have stolen the book for one of the best scenes. Along side an old favorite. Again, wish I could say more. This book was full of people starting to tap into their powers and let loose a bit. I had chills during so many scenes. There was justice and some injustice both being served. The justice far outweighed any bad, though. <br /><br />The plot had taken on such a great route and it also has set up for some truly amazing scenes later on. So many different story arcs are turning out to be way better than I would've thought back when they first made their appearance. So much so that I wish we could start the next book right where we're leaving off, but this is Malazan so I'm pretty sure I'll be waiting until at least book 8 to get some resolution. It's definitely worth the wait, if that's the case.<br /><br />All-in-all, very solid addition to the Malazan series! Based off this book, alone, I'd recommend the whole series. Witness!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4477343865335508758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1687180994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1687180994" />
    <a title="Jenna Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32846944-jenna-kathleen"><img alt="Jenna Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583785298p2/32846944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1687180994?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna Kathleen" href="/user/show/32846944-jenna-kathleen">Jenna Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32846944-jenna-kathleen?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32846944-jenna-kathleen?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32846944-jenna-kathleen?shelf=canadian-authors">canadian-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32846944-jenna-kathleen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1687180994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8513328006752362771">I'm a little sad that I only have 4 books of the main series left - I never want to leave Malaz.<br/><br/>After <i>Midnight Tides</i>, I was so happy to see some familiar faces again. I still loved the 5th book, but this was an extra level of epic to return to the characters I love after some awesome worldbuilding in book 5. <br/><br/>Cotillion is one of the best characters who doesn't even show up that much, but you know he's always working behind the scenes and when he does appear, you can't put the book down.<br/><br/>I love Gan</span>
  <span id="freeText8513328006752362771" style="display:none">I'm a little sad that I only have 4 books of the main series left - I never want to leave Malaz.<br /><br />After <i>Midnight Tides</i>, I was so happy to see some familiar faces again. I still loved the 5th book, but this was an extra level of epic to return to the characters I love after some awesome worldbuilding in book 5. <br /><br />Cotillion is one of the best characters who doesn't even show up that much, but you know he's always working behind the scenes and when he does appear, you can't put the book down.<br /><br />I love Ganoes Paran's character development. At first, when he <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[becomes Master of the Deck, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> he's a bit like a whining child. It's a realistic reaction to a life-altering event that you can't even control. He didn't want or know how to take on all that responsibility, but he has really grown into his role in this book.<br /><br />We have all the favourite Bridgeburners - Kalam and Quick Ben, Fiddler and Bottle as well as some fun new characters in the ranks. Other favourites like Apsalar and Karsa Orlong who are intriguing to follow and create a lot of humour (at least on Karsa's part).<br /><br />The biggest surprise for me was that I really liked Tavore in <i>The Bonehunters.</i> I think that is what really makes Erikson brilliant. He can change your opinion on any character and creates sympathy in you for characters you never thought you could have any interest in.<br /><br />The pacing throughout <i>The Bonehunters</i> was better than previous books, but as always, the ending was beyond expectations. The coolest thing about the ending of this novel is that you have a lot of the characters in previous novels finally coming together and the last 3 or 4 chapters, I did not want to put the book down at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8513328006752362771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1329080117" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1329080117" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1329080117?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780765348838" href="/book/show/2183113.The_Bonehunters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1329080117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16675374240416871818">--- INITIAL THOUGHTS --- <br/><br/>So happy to have finished this up! It's the longest book I've read EVER I believe. <br/>I have a lot of thoughts to sort through before I review this so my review will follow very soon. <br/>Suffice to say it was very very good!<br/><br/>--- FINAL REVIEW ---<br/><br/>So, this book is the book which I was a little intimidated by when I saw the size and this coming from someone who read a LOT of very big books. It's a whopping 1,200 pages, and much as I love the Malazan characters and world I did find </span>
  <span id="freeText16675374240416871818" style="display:none">--- INITIAL THOUGHTS --- <br><br>So happy to have finished this up! It's the longest book I've read EVER I believe. <br>I have a lot of thoughts to sort through before I review this so my review will follow very soon. <br>Suffice to say it was very very good!<br><br>--- FINAL REVIEW ---<br><br>So, this book is the book which I was a little intimidated by when I saw the size and this coming from someone who read a LOT of very big books. It's a whopping 1,200 pages, and much as I love the Malazan characters and world I did find myself baulking a little at the size when I first got it in the post and saw the amount of pages!<br>However, with that said I still thought it was a very good book on the whole and one which I enjoyed a lot. I found myself drawn deeper and deeper into the world of these characters and saw more of the horrors, joys, problems and mysteries as they unfolded before me.<br><br>This book in particular focuses on a lot of convergence of our previous plot lines. <br>Remember the Edur we met in Midnight Tides? This book harks back to more trouble with them.<br>Remember the Bridgeburners? There's still stuff unresolved there.<br>Remember our new Master of the Deck? Well this book brings him back with a will and a vengeance.<br>Remember the terrible struggles we've seen our characters face before? Oh yep, that's definitely back!<br>Remember the Gods who like to meddle? Yeahhh, they're still doing that.<br><br>Basically a lot of the different plot lines which we have so far seen or been focusing on almost exclusively get to come together and join up in various ways in this book which for me marked that this was the turning point of the series... we're over halfway and this monster of a book helped to push us there.<br><br>As for the enjoyment levels whilst reading this I would say that this is a hard one to talk about because whilst I did really adore some of the book (e.g. the sections with the Y'Gatan tunnel and Karsa and other fab characters) I didn't necessarily think it needed to be quite as long as it ended up being. This book has some really dark, miserable and desperate moments and throughout those I was filled with awe and sorrow for our characters. It made me want to give them all hugs and cry along with them, but they're used to the horrors of this world and they know what to do and how far to go to get through some of the worst that Erikson can throw at them.<br><br>The characters in this book included the return of some of my favourites. <br>- We have The Master of the Deck who is being a real badass at times in this book and not only works with the dead and has control of some of the gods, but has some really very redeemable, heartwarming moments too. I liked seeing him step up and not be afraid to embrace his new role and go for it with gusto.<br>- Karsa is a character I have been fully in love with since we first met him and so the return of Karsa is always a fabulous thing in my mind. I love that he's so bloodthirsty and fierce and crass at times, but at other times his compassion and care for the tribes and people of the world do shine through.<br>- I loved seeing Icarium and Mappo back and I have to say that seeing an angry Icarium and a sad Mappo at time made me so emotional and choked up too. They're a fabulous pair and seeing the ways that their stories went made me worry for them all the more.<br>- Seeing Trell come back into the story was also great because since we know his people's past now, due to reading Midnight Tides I like him so, so much more as a character than I did before and I admire the bravery he had in order to leave his tribe and become a wanderer essentially.<br>- Iskarul Pust and his wife had me laughing a lot, they were for sure the comic relief in this book and with the Malazan books you always learn to appreciate the more bizarre creatures because the humour they bring makes you see that maybe there is a little bit of hope in this dark, harsh and lonely world.<br>- Even seeing Cutter and his crew made me intrigued because they were given some pretty interesting challenges to overcome along the way.<br>- Tavore was a character that I have to say I wasn't a fan of to begin with but seeing the way that she handled herself over the course of this book made me rethink and re-evaluate her a little.<br>- Apsalar is a character who has certainly come a long way since when we first met her and seeing her with Telorast and Curdle made me wonder and chuckle a lot too. She's dancing the shadows and working for the Gods, but she's got her own plans and ideas along the way.<br>- Even Kruppe makes a little appearance and I hope that he'll be back in the next few books because I still really enjoy him and his eccentricities. <br><br>There are so many more characters that have an impact or an emotionally charged moment within this book, but if I did I'd go one forever and so those I've mentioned are the most important ones and the ones that I remember and love or feel for the most.<br><br>In terms of the writing style Erikson once more manages to bring to life so many wonderfully thought-provoking scenes and moments with his skill at crafting sentences. He's a genius when it comes to how to fit all the pieces slowly and gradually into place, and he's also very very good at making you question and think like the characters in their situations. I love the darkness and sorrow he can provoke within me, and the fun and wit he can inspire too. By this point in the series I don't think you'd have continued did you not really admire his skills and the way he goes about creating this epic. <br><br>I will say that after having read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/458394.Night_of_Knives__Malazan_Empire___1_" title="Night of Knives (Malazan Empire, #1) by Ian C. Esslemont" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1327981918s/458394.jpg" alt="Night of Knives (Malazan Empire, #1) by Ian C. Esslemont" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> last month which was a very different style of writing but still within the Malazan world this was for sure a big improvement on that. I felt that this book, despite being too long in places, it drew me into the story and forced me to watch and sympathise with everything and everyone. <br><br>On the whole I had mostly ups with this book and a few slightly drawn out moments which means that I can only give it a 4.5*s rather than a 5*s, but I think this may also have been down to the reading mood I was in at the time. I have read a lot of books this month and last and this was by far the longest which meant it felt a lot longer and I noticed the drawn out parts a lot more in comparison to my smaller books. However, if you've enjoyed the rest of the book in this series this is of course a must-read and it's a brilliantly complex continuation and convergence of so many plotlines. I can't wait to see how (the even-longer!!!) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/459064.Reaper_s_Gale__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___7_" title="Reaper's Gale (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #7) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1403011403s/459064.jpg" alt="Reaper's Gale (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #7) by Steven Erikson" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> goes now! A solid 4.5*s :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16675374240416871818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_100008834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100008834" />
    <a title="Duffy Pratt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2729963-duffy-pratt"><img alt="Duffy Pratt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1282095213p2/2729963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100008834?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duffy Pratt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duffy Pratt" href="/user/show/2729963-duffy-pratt">Duffy Pratt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2729963-duffy-pratt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2729963-duffy-pratt?shelf=shared-world">shared-world</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100008834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8430386209333013236">10/10/11 - This series keeps getting better. This book doesn't work as a standalone novel, but that's not too surprising in a book for number six in an ongoing saga. Rather, this one felt to me like two novels in one. First, there is the baptism by fire of the Bonehunters. And then second, there is the Return of the 14th Army to Malaz Island. Both of these sections stand up with anything already in the series. <br/><br/>GRR Martin got famous by killing off a beloved character. He did it once, and since th</span>
  <span id="freeText8430386209333013236" style="display:none">10/10/11 - This series keeps getting better. This book doesn't work as a standalone novel, but that's not too surprising in a book for number six in an ongoing saga. Rather, this one felt to me like two novels in one. First, there is the baptism by fire of the Bonehunters. And then second, there is the Return of the 14th Army to Malaz Island. Both of these sections stand up with anything already in the series. <br /><br />GRR Martin got famous by killing off a beloved character. He did it once, and since then the main characters have been pretty much safe. Not so with Erikson. By now, he's killed off many of his main characters, and I don't have the sense that anyone in these books is at all safe. I have pretty much zero idea who is going to make it through to the end. Also, I've now gotten over Erikson bringing back the dead in these books. It no longer feels to me like Gandalf redux, and is simply a part of his world.<br /><br />The main difficulty I'm now having with these books is my level of confusion with some of the characters motives. Almost every character we see in these books is both a puppet and a puppet-master. They are all manipulating things according to their own plans, while at the same time being manipulated by others. This makes things fascinating, and it makes the characters very intricate, but it also keeps me more than a little disoriented at times. For example, its not easy for me to figure out the relationship between Quick Ben and Shadowthrone. <br /><br />For that reason, my poor simpleton brain gets a strange feeling of relief whenever Karsa is on the scene. He's refreshingly blunt, and unmoved by the manipulations of others. More than anyone else in this book, he is simply his own man. He's a bastard, but a pure one. On the opposite end of the spectrum, I suppose, is Quick Ben. Instead of being his own man, he's twelve people literally rolled into one. He deals and double-deals with gods. At no point in these books have I been fully clear where he stands, nor with whom he is truly allied (except probably Kalam). He's an amazing character, and very cool, but I find him to be very confusing.<br /><br /><br />When I'm done with this series, I may have to go back and re-do my ratings for the individual books. Even though I haven't given any of the books five stars yet, the series as a whole is shaping up to be a five star series.<br /><br />Reread 9/14/13<br /><br />OK, I'm doing my re-read before finishing the series. I did this for some other series, rereading the series as each new book came out. Then I decided never to start a series until the author was finished with it. That's a vow I've already broken, both accidentally and deliberately, but I still think its a pretty good rule of thumb. Now that we are through book six, I'm getting pretty excited that we are only two books away from new territory for me.<br /><br />I got very frustrated at two points in this book. First, there's a conversation between Paran and Hood. During the conversation Paran asks Hood what he really wants in exchange for a big favor. Hood tells him, and the narrator hides the information from us. There's an enormous amount of stuff in this series that you have to remember and store away. There are connections you need to make on your own. But usually, you don't have the narrator deliberately thumbing his nose at the reader. And for the life of me, I can't figure out what Erikson is gaining by deliberately hiding this stuff. <br /><br />My other frustration arose from trying to figure out what Laseen is doing. If you assume that she still has a firm grasp on her power, then her actions make no sense. So, the only conclusion I can draw is that she's lost her grip on her power. Somehow she let Mallick Rel and Korbolo Dom subvert her authority. This should have been a great story on its own, but here it is simply elided.<br /><br />From another standpoint, the elision makes sense. I was expecting a book about the Malazan Empire, and while the books are the Malazan Books of the Fallen, the story they tell does not center on the Malaz Empire. Instead, the story Erikson is telling deals with the clash between the gods, and how some mortals get involved in that clash and influence the outcome. The Empire is decidedly secondary. <br /><br />Here, the story is how the Bonehunters become its own, independent functioning unit, and its a great story. The seige at Y'Ghatan is a remarkable set piece. The conflagration itself is done amazingly well, but the aftermath in the tunnels underneath the city is even better. Later, there is a set piece where dozens of jade meteorites, all filled with millions of souls, comes crashing to the earth, threatening to destroy the world. Here, we finally get to see what the true meaning of "shield anvil" as Heboric catches and absorbs all that energy into himself and saves the world. <br /><br />The first time through the book, I didn't understand this passage at all. There's only so much of the book I could focus on at any time, so there were fairly wide swaths that I just let roll over me. The same thing goes for the entire involvement of the Eresal. This time, I have more appreciation for what Erikson is doing on the more cosmic levels, and its truly extraordinary, and unlike any other fantasy I've read.<br /><br />Then, despite my frustration with the motivations of the Empress, the finale is amazingly well done. There are so many different things going on at once, and they are all done almost perfectly. The last two chapters are a tour de force. And Erikson does this while keeping everything fairly grey (or should I say shadowy). For example, Pearl is functionally a villain, leading the assassins who are trying to kill Kalam, Tavore and T'Amber. And he uses dishonorable means to poison Kalam. And yet, it pretty much tears my guts out when his lover finds him dying and has to put him out of his misery. Conversely, T'Amber seems like a true hero and a badass, and then its revealed that she's been possessed by a "good" god, and all I can do is feel terrible for a person that we never even got to know, and to have some reserved doubts for a god who I basically thought was a good guy.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8430386209333013236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17162850211551722059" style="display:none">Okay I finished this quite awhile ago and I never wrote a review because I have no idea how to.<br /><br />So much happens and there are so many story arcs, lines and characters that I seriously had a hard time keeping up. What I can say is that again people I really liked died :(, people I really hated lived and there was not a happy ending for anyone in the story.<br /><br />I think I lost interest a little in the middle of this book. It really isn't the books fault all the stories are just so dense and full details that go with other details that you really have to pay a lot of attention and I just didn't have the time I needed to devote to that. I mean if you have to read a forum after ever chapter to understand the implications of that chapter it starts to feel more like homework than fun.<br /><br />I am taking a series break. I'm just really more excited about rereading The Stormlight Archives and some other things that aren't quite so dense right now. I really want to finish the series but my mindset isn't where it needs to be to do that now.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14065335520032112223">One of the best Malazan books so far. This is the first book from the series which has a very gripping middle part. Finally no new races, places, characters in the beginning; it jumps right in the middle of action. My only minor complain: people still wander around the desert aimlessly (what is it about the holy desert Raraku that makes people do so?). Mercifully, it takes a small part of the book. My (fairly) major complain: one of the characters died an almost meaningless death almost being a </span>
  <span id="freeText14065335520032112223" style="display:none">One of the best Malazan books so far. This is the first book from the series which has a very gripping middle part. Finally no new races, places, characters in the beginning; it jumps right in the middle of action. My only minor complain: people still wander around the desert aimlessly (what is it about the holy desert Raraku that makes people do so?). Mercifully, it takes a small part of the book. My (fairly) major complain: one of the characters died an almost meaningless death almost being a casualty. The problem with it is that we have a lot of his inner thoughts during at least two other books for this person to be killed without accomplished almost anything. I failed to connect to this person, so that was the point of long sections for his POV? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I am talking about Heboric Ghost Hands <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />On to the plot: Adjunct Tavore chases the last surviving commander of the rebels across the desert. It seems victory is assured; there is only one minor problem: it seems a lot of people and quite a few gods are not interested in this victory, quite the opposite. The parts about soldiers of the army are really, really good and interesting; they try to remain human beings despite the constant struggle for survival. <br /><br />I did not expect the betrayals in the end of this book; it made a very exciting ride with 5 solid star rating.</span>

<div id="review_1671842632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1671842632" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2613919-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483904179p2/2613919.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1671842632?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/2613919-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1671842632" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4031308779033625356">5 Stars <br/><br/>The Bonehunters is a perfect addition to the Malazan Book of the Fallen series. This is the sixth story of the series and a very heavy one. It is literally huge and comes in at over 1200 pages in length (paperback). It is also very heavy due to its complexity. This book would not work as a standalone and is elevated by how well it brings the previous novels into this one. Difficult does not even begin to describe it. <br/><br/>I found myself torn over and over again between feeling exhilarated and</span>
  <span id="freeText4031308779033625356" style="display:none">5 Stars <br /><br />The Bonehunters is a perfect addition to the Malazan Book of the Fallen series. This is the sixth story of the series and a very heavy one. It is literally huge and comes in at over 1200 pages in length (paperback). It is also very heavy due to its complexity. This book would not work as a standalone and is elevated by how well it brings the previous novels into this one. Difficult does not even begin to describe it. <br /><br />I found myself torn over and over again between feeling exhilarated and thrilled with the action, the writing, the return of beloved characters and also frustrated, angry, and lost with the sheer complexity of the story, the countless number of points of view, and so many characters that I often had to back track and look them up on wiki to set things straight. The Bonehunters has just about every character ever mentioned in the previous five novels covering the alphabet I am sure.<br /><br />The character list from the front of the book and also from the wiki page.<br /><br /><br />"Ahlrada Ahn, a Tiste Andii spy among the Tiste Edur<br />* Apsalar, an assassin<br />B<br />* Balm, Sergeant, 14th Army<br />* Banaschar, an ex-priest of D'rek<br />* Barathol Mekhar, a blacksmith<br />* Blistig, Fist, Malazan division commander<br />* Bottle, 14th Army<br />* Braven Tooth, Master Sergeant, 14th Army<br />* Brethless, a city guard in Kartool<br />C<br />* Chaur, a villager<br />* Crump, 14th Army<br />* Curdle, a spirit<br />* Cutter, once Crokus of Darujhistan<br />* Cuttle, 14th Army<br />D<br />* Deadsmell, Corporal, 14th Army<br />* Dejim Nebrahl, a D'ivers T'rolbharal of the First Empire<br />* Dunsparrow, Captain, Y'Ghatan city guard<br />E<br />* Ebron, 14th Army<br />F<br />* Faradan Sort, Captain, 14th Army<br />* Feather Witch, a Letherii slave<br />* Felisin the Younger, refugee from Raraku<br />* Fiddler/Strings, Sergeant, 14th Army<br />* Futhgar, a Corporal in Onearm's Host<br />G<br />* Ganath, a Jaghut<br />* Gesler, Sergeant, 14th Army<br />* Greyfrog, a demon<br />* Grub, a foundling<br />* Gumble, his critic<br />H<br />* Hayrith, a villager<br />* Heboric Ghost Hands, Destriant of Treach<br />* Hellian, a sergeant in the city of Kartool<br />* Hurlochel, an outrider in Onearm's Host<br />I<br />* Ibra Gholan, a T'lan Imass<br />* Icarium, a Jhag<br />* Iskaral Pust, a priest of Shadow<br />K<br />* Kalam Mekhar, an assassin<br />* Karpolan Demesand, Trygalle Trade Guild<br />* Karsa Orlong, a Teblor warrior<br />* Keneb, Fist, Malazan division commander<br />* Kindly, Captain, Ashok Regiment, 14th Army<br />* Koryk, 14th Army<br />* Kulat, a villager<br />L<br />* Laseen, Empress of the Malazan Empire<br />* Leoman of the Flails, last leader of the rebellion<br />* Lostara Yil, aide to Pearl<br />* Lutes, 14th Army<br />M<br />* Mappo Runt, a Trell<br />* Masan Gilani, 14th Army<br />* Maybe, 14th Army<br />* Minala, commander of the Company of Shadow<br />* Mogora, a D'ivers<br />* Monok Ochem, a T'lan Imass bonecaster<br />N<br />* Nether, a Wickan witch with the Malazan Army<br />* Nil, a Wickan warlock with the Malazan Army<br />* Nok, Admiral of the Imperial Fleet<br />* Noto Boil, company cutter (healer) in Onearm's Host<br />* Nulliss, a villager<br />O<br />* Onrack the Broken, an unbound T'lan Imass<br />* Ormulogun, an artist<br />P<br />* Pearl, a Claw<br />* Pores, Lieutenant, Ashok Regiment, 14th Army<br />Q<br />* Quick Ben, High Mage in the Fourteenth Army<br />R<br />* Robello, 14th Army<br />* Rythe Bude, a Fist in Onearm's Host<br />S<br />* Samar Dev, a witch of Ugarat<br />* Sathbaro Rangar, Arapay warlock<br />* Scillara, refugee from Raraku<br />* Sinn, 14th Army<br />* Smiles, 14th Army<br />* Spite, a Soletaken and sister to Lady Envy<br />* Stormy, Corporal, 14th Army<br />* Sweetcreek, a Captain in Onearm's Host<br />T<br />* T'amber, Tavore's aide<br />* Tak, an armourer in Malaz City[1] ♦<br />* Taralack Veed, a Gral and agent of the the Nameless Ones<br />* Tarr, Corporal, 14th Army<br />* Tavore, Adjunct, commander of the Fourteenth Army<br />* Taxilian, an interpreter<br />* Telorast, a spirit<br />* Temul, Fist, Malazan division commander<br />* Tene Baralta, Fist, Malazan division commander<br />* Throatslitter, 14th Army<br />* Tomad Sengar, a Tiste Edur<br />* Torahaval Delat, a priestess of Poliel<br />* Touchy, a city guard in Kartool<br />* Tugg, Sergeant, 14th Army<br />* Trull Sengar, a Tiste Edur<br />U<br />Urb, a city guard in Kartool<br />V<br />* Varat Taun, Captain under Twilight's Command<br />Y<br />* Yan Tovis (Twilight), Atri-Preda, commander of Letherii forces"<br /><br />As if this massive list of characters and points of view isn't hard enough, many of them have more than one name or were called a different name previously. It is a testament to just how good Erikson's storytelling and writing is, that I not only found a way to navigate through the countless pov's, I actually loved every minute of it. This is a long read that is made longer if you cannot designate long periods of time to read as you are constantly play catch up on the who is who? Thank God for Wikipedia.<br /><br /><br /><br />The Bonehunters is a very dark and action filled novel brimming with magic, swords, Warrens, and creatures. This is fantasy at it's finest. All others will strive to live up to the world created in the Book of the Fallen. It basically has no equal.<br /><br />I loved the return of so many amazing characters. The Gods and their machinations shine. The magic is incredible. If you have read the series so far, you already know what to expect and will surely read this one as you move on.<br /><br />A giant story with an even larger cast. This changes everything.<br /><br />Simply amazing!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4031308779033625356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_312980574" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312980574" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312980574?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8260815-bonehunters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312980574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9003301642886696247">I could again go into great length about how Erikson brings his world to life in deep and detailed world building, or how the reread of each of the Malazan books is a vastly superior experience to the initial read given the density of information that is missed on round one – but it gets a little repetitive after book six as far as reviews go and if you have got this far you are probably already in love with the series anyway. So I’ll try and stick to some of the basics of plot and theme for tho</span>
  <span id="freeText9003301642886696247" style="display:none">I could again go into great length about how Erikson brings his world to life in deep and detailed world building, or how the reread of each of the Malazan books is a vastly superior experience to the initial read given the density of information that is missed on round one – but it gets a little repetitive after book six as far as reviews go and if you have got this far you are probably already in love with the series anyway. So I’ll try and stick to some of the basics of plot and theme for those looking to see what’s up next after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345299.Midnight_Tides__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___5_" title="Midnight Tides (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #5) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a>.<br /><br />In broad strokes this book is a continuation of the events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55398.House_of_Chains__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___4_" title="House of Chains (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #4) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Chains</a> so we are back to Seven Cities, reuniting with Tavore’s 14th army as they pursue the remnants of the Apocalypse Rebellion. This leads us to the key chapter of the book(quite early at Ch7) which deals with the battle at Y’Ghatan where the 14th is forged in the fires of battle into “The Bonehunters.” <br /><br />This chapter spans over 10% of the book and things get very intense in term of battle sequences, Apocalyptic scenes and stories of survival. We have acts of both heroism and cowardice, lives given meaningfully as well as lives wasted in the random roll of the dice. Even though it’s fantasy and therefore typically lowtech – the inclusion of Moranth munitions launched to devastating effect via flat bow gave the fight a very contemporary feel. <br /><br />On top of all that we have gods conscripting mortals for the expanding war of ascendants and the theme of gods and mortals being mutually bound to each other continues. We will also walk the underworld with Ganoes Paran, we will see Bridgeburners both alive and dead. We will continue on with Icarium’s journey. We also check in on Karsa. The Tiste Edur are still out there trying to take the Throne of Shadow and the First Throne of the Imass while also searching for a champion that can continue the Edur Emperor’s cycle of death and resurrection. We learn more about dragons and their relationship to the warrens, there will be things unleashed that are better off left chained and buried, and more. <br /><br />All this will bring us to a convergence that will spill over and race through the streets and alleys of the Empire's spiritual heart, leaving us out of breath in a show down of Tooth and Claw, Assassin and Foot Soldier, Blood and Poison, Shadow and Chaos.<br /><br /><br />5 stars Locked and Loaded <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9003301642886696247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/744602-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357149372p2/744602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49635997?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/744602-lori">Lori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49635997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1091798424231801804">It's useless. I keep intending to take a break between these and read something else that I've been eagerly anticipating, but the fact of the matter is I'm addicted to this series. And it's all I want to read. So why deny myself?<br/><br/>Finally finished! I haven't had much reading time this whole past month, and I have been so so frustrated, because this is such a marvelous addition that continues to satisfy and feed my obsession with this series. Also, it does meander a bit in the middle so it's not as</span>
  <span id="freeText1091798424231801804" style="display:none">It's useless. I keep intending to take a break between these and read something else that I've been eagerly anticipating, but the fact of the matter is I'm addicted to this series. And it's all I want to read. So why deny myself?<br /><br />Finally finished! I haven't had much reading time this whole past month, and I have been so so frustrated, because this is such a marvelous addition that continues to satisfy and feed my obsession with this series. Also, it does meander a bit in the middle so it's not as tight as the previous one.<br /><br />Erikson is so gifted at making me care about so many characters. Who would have thought I'd be so distraught about an assassin? And that I loved someone called Lifestealer? It's because these characters have so much depth, and I get furious about how they are manipulated. Has Laseen lost it? Will the Trell reach his goal? So many things that make me want to immediately delve into the next book, Erikson has left me hanging! And I've promised to read another book for a group I'm in. Can I do that? I'll give the other a fair shot, but I dunno....<br /><br />The females are just as good as the males - strong, powerful, I love that. <br /><br />These books are violent, so not for the faint of heart. However, Erikson is very clear with his philosophies - no, not lecturing at all but through the action and the characters - so we are appalled by much of it, yet fascinated by the action. He has alot to say about inflexibility, xenophobia, revision of history for politics sake, friendship, all of that gooooood stuff.<br /><br />These books are remarkable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1091798424231801804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8363307438268431684" style="display:none">Click, clack is the sound of the bones I've bound to my hair. Clack, click is the sound of the bones on my clothes. As I march in tune with my fellow Fallen, I hear Fiddler's song chime on the wind. With tears in my eyes I move forward through ever-changing warrens of grief and wonder and magic. I'll follow the Adjunct now, whereever she leads us, however the opposition, cause I'm one of hers now. A Bonehunter.<br /><br />Oh, the things I've seen in the past months. I saw the soldiers from Genabackis united with friends from the Seven Cities.<br />I saw the chaotic force of the Tiste Edur clash with the known world. What is their aim, to what use are we to their emperor, I cannot say.<br />I saw the universe weep, when Mappo's and Icarium's fate went down a road so strangely unfamiliar, but inevitable. Damn you, Nameless Ones! Be damned once and twice and thrice!<br />I was there at Y'Ghatan. And if you just think of that place as Dassem Ultor's final fight, you, my friend, were not. <br />And beware the slayer of children! As Karsa Orlong is not finished with us yet. Do you feel his stare on you, the need to witness and grow from it? <br />And now I bury my hands in the bones of the empire with a taste of salted water in my mouth. Laseen, what have you down? Is it truly the gods, who make the rules or am I responsible? Are we as mortals just dictating our gods with our own expectations. Do we bind them by ritual and sacrifice into the beings they are?<br /><br />And I haven't told you of Apsalar, my poor poor Apsalar. How beautiful it was to see you dance again.<br /><br />So, dear reader, what did you expect? Did you truly think it was possible to review this book? Do you think it would fit in words?<br />You need to feel this world to understand the impossibility of such a task. It's 1000 pages of emotion bursting through your skull. <br />So, step forward, I'll throw you a bone. Bind it to your hair or clothes and hear its promise in the wind, click clack, clack click...on every single page. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1228336497" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1228336497" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7022024-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470679918p2/7022024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1228336497?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/7022024-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19746283-the-bonehunters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=epics">epics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1228336497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9974035683417017036">As much as I made fun of the previous book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1202428310?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midnight Tides</a>, as being the quintessential Malazan book (huge new cast of characters, place we had never been to before, time period before the main arc, etc.), The Bonehunters struck me as a very conventional, but still quite excellent, novel. We returned to see many, many familiar faces from past books. It was so strange recognize just about every main character, know what was going on, and understand the dynamics of their respective situations. Lik</span>
  <span id="freeText9974035683417017036" style="display:none">As much as I made fun of the previous book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1202428310?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Tides</a>, as being the quintessential Malazan book (huge new cast of characters, place we had never been to before, time period before the main arc, etc.), The Bonehunters struck me as a very conventional, but still quite excellent, novel. We returned to see many, many familiar faces from past books. It was so strange recognize just about every main character, know what was going on, and understand the dynamics of their respective situations. Like I said, very un-Malazanish.<br /><br />This book felt like it was mostly about rearranging the proverbial pieces on the board. By the end of the book most of the characters are well on their way to somewhere else with a bit of a stop over in the plot. While there were certainly some titanic events, I felt like this book didn't quite have the same end of book umph as the previous installments. Don't get me wrong, I still greatly enjoy this book, it just read as a much more conventional novel than the rest of the series.<br /><br />The titles of the books thus far have fallen into two categories: description of something in the book (Gardens of the Moon, Deadhouse Gates) or the overriding theme of the book (Memories of Ice, House of Chains, Midnight Tides). The Bonehunters falls squarely into the former category, not really giving insight into an overall theme of this book. Like I said before, this was very much about re-positioning characters (both spatially and relationally) instead of ruminating on the invisible chains that bind us (Hour of Chains) or the invisible social structures that mold our outlook (Midnight Tides).<br /><br />This book touches on just about every previous plot line in the series, giving us a nice, linear progression of each of them. They don't all overlap (I mean, this is still a Malazan book, we can't expect Erikson to completely kowtow to convention) but all have a few new characters nicely sprinkled in and see a nice bit of advancement. Two things that did stand out is that we saw a lot more of Cotillion and Shadowthrone, and they were awesome, and Ganoes Paran as Master of the Deck was flipping fantastic. <br /><br />If I was a strong theme running through this book I would say it is this: "When elephants fight, it is the grass that suffers". This book sees a bunch of gods taking a much more direct hand in the mortal realms, almost always to the detriment of the mortals of said realm. <i>"Whether we worship or not, it is mortal blood that will soak the earth."</i><br /><br />But there were plenty of other things going on not directly related to this clash of elephants. All in all, though, a very satisfying next step that sets up some amazingly awesome potential clashes in the next book.<br /><br />All that being said, Erikson did not disappoint on the prose and ideas this book contained. So without further ado:<br /><br /><b>You know, Imperialism isn't THAT bad sometimes</b>: <i>More than the cult of d'rek had been crushed, after all. Slavery was abolished, the execution pits had been scoured clean and permanently sealed. There was even a building hosting a score of misguided altruists who adopted lame dogs.</i><br /><br /><b>In case you forgot how awesome Karsa was</b>:<i> "These matters must be brought to the Falah'd." He faced Karsa again. "You will stay this night at the Inn of the Wood?"<br />"I shall, although it is not made of wood, and so it should be called Inn of the Brick."</i><br /><br /><b>Speaking of awesome characters, Iskaral Pust still is</b>: <i>"...The point is, I am well advised to remind myself, as I am now doing, the point is, he summoned me. And so here I am. Rightful servant. Loyal. Well, more or less loyal. Trustworthy. Most of the time. Modest and respectful, always. To all outward appearances, and what is outward in appearance is all that matters in this and every other world. Isn't it? Smile! Grimace. Look helpful!"</i><br /><br /><b>Heck, let's just throw Greyfrog into the mix</b>: <i><br /><b>Greyfrog</b>: Belated observation. Grubs, there in the dark reaches of the nest. Nest? Bemused. Hive? Nest.<br /><b>Cutter</b>: You didn't. You did.<br /><b>Greyfrog</b>: Irate is their common state, I niw believe. Breaking open their cave made them more so. We clashed in buzzing disagreement. I fared the worse, I think.<br /><b>Cutter</b>: Black wasps?<br /><b>Greyfrog</b>: Tilt head, query. Black? Breaded reply, why yes, they were. Black. Rhetorical, was that significant?<br /><b>Cutter</b>: Be glad you're a demon. Two of three stings from those will kill a grown man. Ten will kill a harse.<br /><b>Greyfrog</b>: A horse - we had those - you had them. I was forced to run. Horse. Large four-legged animal. Succulent meat.<br /><b>Cutter</b>: People tend to ride them until they drop. then we eat them.<br /><b>Greyfrog</b>: Multiple uses, excellent and unwasteful.</i><br /><br /><b>And who can forget Kruppe</b>: <i> The Gods, dear precious friend of Kruppe's! they are at war, yes? Terrible thing, war. Terrible things, gods. The two, together, ah, most terribler."</i><br /><br /><b>Best Bromance in all the realms</b>:<i><br /><b>Icarium</b>: None of my desires surprise you, do they? It is no exaggeration that you know my mind better than I. Would that you were a women.<br /><b>Mappo</b>: Were I a woman, Icarium, I would have serious concerns about your taste in women.<br /><b>Icarium</b>: Granted, you are somewhat hairy. Bristly, in fact. Given your girth, I believe you capable of wrestling a bull bhederin to the ground.</i><br /><br /><b>The second best bromance in the realms</b>: <i>"My frined has seen better days," Trull Sengar said, reaching out to slap Onrack on the back. The thump the blow made was hollow, raising dust, and something clattered down within the warrior's chest. "Oh," said the Triste Edur, "did that do something bad."<br />"No," Onrack replied. "The broken point of a spear. It had been lodged in bone."<br />"Was it irritating you?"<br />"Only the modest sound it made when I walked. Thank you, Trull Sengar."</i><br /><br /><b>Getting real sick of your all knowing shit Heboric</b>:<i><br /><b>Cutter</b>: Heboric, can you check the outbuilding for feed?<br /><b>Heboric</b>: The livestock were never let out. It's been days. The heat killed them all. A dozen goats, two mules.<br /><b>Cutter</b>: Just see if there's any feed.</i><br /><br /><b>We will only endure animal antics for so long</b>: <i>"There's a falcon's nest on the ledge of that tower, the copper-sheathed one."<br />"That is no falcon."<br />"You are right. It's a bokh'aral that found the abandoned nest to its liking. It carries up armfuls of rotting fruit and it spends the morning dropping them on people in the streets below."<br />"It appears to be snarling..."<br />"That would be laughter. It is forever driven to bouts of hilarity."<br />"Ah - no, that wasn't a fruit. It was a brick."<br />"Oh, unfortunate. Someone will be sent to kill it now. After all, only people are allowed to throw bricks at people."</i><br /><br /><b>At least he knows where they are coming from</b>: <i>...the beast had taken to holding its breathe, chest swollen in an effort to keep the strap loose, likely hoping Paran would slide off from its back at some perfectly inopportune time. Horses were reluctant companions in so many human escapades, disasters, and foibles - Paran could not resent the animal's well-earned belligerence.</i><br /><br /><b>Deep theological thoughts with an assassin</b>: <i>"That depends, I suppose. On whether the god worshipped is, by virtue of being worshipped, in turn beholden to the worshipper. If that god isn't - if there is no moral compact - then your answer is "no", it's not a betrayal... If, on the other hand, a moral compact does exist between god and worshipper, then each and every denial represents a betrayal-"<br />"Assuming that which is asked of that god is in itself bound to a certain morality."<br />"True. A husband praying his wife dies in some terrible accident so that he can marry his mistress, for example,is hardly something any self-respecting god would acquiesce to, or assist in."<br />"And if the wife is a tyrant who beats their children?"<br />"Then a truly just god would act without the necessity for prayer." </i><br /><br /><b>What if the tail wags the dog?</b>: <i>"...when inequity burgeons into violent conflagration, the gods themselves are helpless. The gods cease to lead - they can but follow, dragged by the will of their worshippers. Now, suppose gods to be essentially moral entities - that is, possessing and indeed manifestly representing a particular ethos - well, then, such moral considerations become the first victim in the war. Unless that god chooses to defend him or herself form his or her own believers."</i><br /><br /><b>Practical atheism in a world with gods and monsters</b>: <i>"I mean, I don't see much reason behind following any god or goddess. If you're worth their interest, they use you. I know about being used, and most of the rewards are anything but, even if they look good at the time."</i><br /><br />And obviously many, many more delightful pearls of prose. Can't wait to see how this all turns out!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9974035683417017036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44380498?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765310" href="/book/show/11504597-the-bonehunters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=2012-read-owned">2012-read-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=read-owned-hardcover">read-owned-hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=malazan-books">malazan-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44380498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15248362612349044523">3.75 stars.<br/><br/>I almost dropped it to 3 stars, as there were lots of WTF moments and confusing drawn out parts. In truth, this book could have probably been half the length and been just as good (as long as it was the right half).<br/><br/>The Bonehunters were great. Paran, Kalam and Quick Ben, and Karsa Orlong. Oh, and I loved <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[our first real interaction with Laseen, the Empress.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Badass stuff. <br/><br/>When this book was good, it was fantastic. When not as good, it was like a big, long </span>
  <span id="freeText15248362612349044523" style="display:none">3.75 stars.<br /><br />I almost dropped it to 3 stars, as there were lots of WTF moments and confusing drawn out parts. In truth, this book could have probably been half the length and been just as good (as long as it was the right half).<br /><br />The Bonehunters were great. Paran, Kalam and Quick Ben, and Karsa Orlong. Oh, and I loved <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[our first real interaction with Laseen, the Empress.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Badass stuff. <br /><br />When this book was good, it was fantastic. When not as good, it was like a big, long "huh?"<br /><br />I can't in good conscience recommend or push this series anymore. Not to the unsuspecting, at least. It will fit a groove with some, but certainly not all.<br /><br />I loved the first book, though many say it's tough. I didn't have any problem with it.<br /><br />The second and third books blew me away, they were so good.<br /><br />The fourth was a monkey spank. Let's be honest.<br /><br />The fifth was better again, but still a lot of "huh"? going on.<br /><br />The sixth was a continuation of the monkey spank from Book 4, so that was much of the problem. Honestly, half of this book could go to the shit pile and not be missed. Lots of b.s. wtfery, and each book seems to pile it on rather than clear things up.<br /><br />That said, when it's good, it's <i>really fucking good</i>.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_816400744" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/816400744" />
    <a title="Nate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6803829-nate"><img alt="Nate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413944642p2/6803829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/816400744?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nate" href="/user/show/6803829-nate">Nate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer816400744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer623173558516379390">RE-READ REVIEW: Reading this massive fucker a second time has definitely cemented it as one of my favorite entries in this series. I haven’t finished the series yet but I’m pretty sure Seven Cities is gonna stay my favorite Malazan setting/continent/arc, and thusly probably my favorite fantasy setting/continent/arc. The whole thing just oozes ancient history, unforgiving terrain, buried cities, religious fanaticism, unending strife and conflict, etc. SO. MUCH. GOOD. SHIT. The story itself was ye</span>
  <span id="freeText623173558516379390" style="display:none">RE-READ REVIEW: Reading this massive fucker a second time has definitely cemented it as one of my favorite entries in this series. I haven’t finished the series yet but I’m pretty sure Seven Cities is gonna stay my favorite Malazan setting/continent/arc, and thusly probably my favorite fantasy setting/continent/arc. The whole thing just oozes ancient history, unforgiving terrain, buried cities, religious fanaticism, unending strife and conflict, etc. SO. MUCH. GOOD. SHIT. The story itself was yet another stunning entry in the saga of the Malazan struggle to hang onto the continent in the face of a truly epic religious rebellion that started in <i>Deadhouse Gates</i>. It was packed full of gripping stories big and small, and that’s all I really wanna say about the plot itself. Just hinting at where shit might go is really unavoidably spoilery for this kind of book. Last thing: I’m pretty sure this contains the funniest moment in the books thus far in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the scene with Stormy shitting his life out over the rail of the <i>Silanda</i> while Captain Kindly retches most hilariously at the sight. See, the Erikson humor with replacement-vagina-monsters and hundreds of Malazan marines shitting over rails is so much funnier than when he’s got his tryhard droll English humor hat on with Tehol &amp; Bugg...at least for me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I NEVER SAID I WAS MATURE!<br><br>ORIGINAL REVIEW: So thus far I've perceived three main threads of the story, broken up by the continents on which they take place (more or less); Genabackis, Seven Cities, and Lether. There's kind of a tertiary thread on Malaz Island going on but yeah, three main ones. Originally, these separate threads took up whole books but we have a significant consolidation going on between the first and second threads, with a good bit of the third one thrown in as well. This makes <i>The Bonehunters</i> a unique entry, and a relatively easy one to get into. There's few of your favorite characters that won't show up in this one...but I guess with such a ridiculously huge cast that could mean like 20 people and a god or two.<br><br>I know for a lot of Erikson fans including myself the Seven Cities plotline has been one of the most memorable. If you are one of those people then you'll probably like this one. The aftershocks of the Chain of Dogs are steadily bringing back the nightmare visions of <i>Deadhouse Gates</i> in unpredictable ways. Some of the moments in this book rank with the most shocking we've witnessed on the continent thus far. It's hard to explain to people how fucking intense these books can be. It can sound like rote fantasy if not properly explained, but even if they are familiar elements Erikson is dedicated to using them in pursuit of this creepily real and immaculately detailed vision of a world none of us would really wanna live in.<br><br>And that cast I mentioned earlier is still bursting with varied, colorful characters. With such a massive group of people to work with you're gonna have characters that never take off or are explored or developed or just have minor parts to play--relatively inconsequential. What always surprises me with Erikson is how few there are of these people. Everyone has their own spark of life and color. With most series, people are gonna generally agree on who their favorites are. This one is a bit more unpredictable than that. Erikson's willingness to really dissect what makes them tick definitely facilitates that. They're all truly different people with different motives. Of course, not everyone's motives are clear to the reader.<br><br>Allow me to complain about something for a bit...the atrocious covers of these books, which are echoed in a million other fantasy series. Series and authors like this deserve better. This isn't limited to fantasy, this unfortunately extends to most genre fiction. It's unfortunate the publishers don't consider hiring an artist with even a passing knowledge of the content of the book. Google did reassure me in the form of one of the newer special edition covers of <i>Deadhouse Gates</i>: (MAJOR SPOILERS FOR SAID BOOK)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393071868i/8657847._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>That</i> is more like it! Also, the apparently Bulgarian cover for same book is awesome, if significantly cheesier than the other one:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393072005i/8657859._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>See? Even at their cheesiest the Bulgarians do good artwork. Why can't we, fellow Americans? NO COUNTRY MUST EVER BEST US AT ANYTHING, ESPECIALLY COVER ART FOR SEMI-OBSCURE FANTASY SERIES!!! Although I always imagined Leoman as more sketchy junkie guy than badass armored warrior.<br><br>Anyways...this was another fantastic book in this most epic of epic fantasies and the ending demands you continue with the next one as soon as possible. The shape of the story is finally starting to be revealed and I think it's gonna continue to be a seminal work. It even made me excited for my impending second encounter with Esslemont, who kind of turned me off with <i>Night of Knives</i>. I really don't see someone who's enjoyed the series up to this point being disappointed in any way, shape or form...but stranger things have happened.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="623173558516379390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zFr9KX76Rs4PsMF1jHPZRtJ2O16RJvTiA6jvdEkI3u0IBD8jKe1H4I6f1Xn0XJiheEYiD5iZDh+689343ocOYw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IcIxyvDuCyAhXisdRlZWnLMr1CbnIbN4AOEhx3GRk7jlnPPAp/kKDqBxPxE+eRd7GRvNd+6eSYW5uhNL5h5DNg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

But the slums boil over with a rage that all the money in the world cannot control.\n\nThe age of the machine dawns, but the age of magic refuses to die. With the help of the mad hillwoman Isern-i-Phail, Rikke struggles to control the blessing, or the curse, of the Long Eye. Glimpsing the future is one thing, but with the guiding hand of the First of the Magi still pulling the strings, changing it will be quite another...\n<\/span>\n  <a       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/3898723-the-bonehunters">Quotes from The Bonehunters</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;There is something profoundly cynical, my friends, in the notion of paradise after death. The lure is evasion. The promise is excusative. One need not accept responsibility for the world as it is, and by extension, one need do nothing about it. To strive for change, for true goodness in this mortal world, one must acknowledge and accept, within one's own soul, that this mortal reality has purpose in itself, that its greatest value is not for us, but for our children and their children. To view life as but a quick passage alone a foul, tortured path – made foul and tortured by our own indifference – is to excuse all manner of misery and depravity, and to exact cruel punishment upon the innocent lives to come.<br /><br />I defy this notion of paradise beyond the gates of bone. If the soul truly survives the passage, then it behooves us – each of us, my friends – to nurture a faith in similitude: what awaits us is a reflection of what we leave behind, and in the squandering of our mortal existence, we surrender the opportunity to learn the ways of goodness, the practice of sympathy, empathy, compassion and healing – all passed by in our rush to arrive at a place of glory and beauty, a place we did not earn, and most certainly do not deserve.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/200281-there-is-something-profoundly-cynical-my-friends-in-the-notion">218 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Show me a god that does not demand mortal suffering.<br />Show me a god that celebrates diversity, a celebration that embraces even non-believers, and is not threatened by them.<br />Show me a god that understands the meaning of peace. In life, not in death.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/566740-show-me-a-god-that-does-not-demand-mortal-suffering">213 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/3898723-the-bonehunters">More quotes&hellip;</a>
